from sklearn import datasets
import numpy

x_sparse, y = datasets.load_svmlight_file('diabetes')
x = x_sparse.todense()

print('Shape of x: ' + str(x.shape))
print('Shape of y: ' + str(y.shape))

Shape of x: (768, 8)
Shape of y: (768,)
In [2]:
# partition the data to training and test sets
n = x.shape[0]
n_train = int(numpy.ceil(n * 0.8))
n_test = n - n_train

rand_indices = numpy.random.permutation(n)
train_indices = rand_indices[0:n_train]
test_indices = rand_indices[n_train:n]

x_train = x[train_indices, :]
x_test = x[test_indices, :]
y_train = y[train_indices].reshape(n_train, 1)
y_test = y[test_indices].reshape(n_test, 1)

print('Shape of x_train: ' + str(x_train.shape))
print('Shape of x_test: ' + str(x_test.shape))
print('Shape of y_train: ' + str(y_train.shape))
print('Shape of y_test: ' + str(y_test.shape))

Shape of x_train: (615, 8)
Shape of x_test: (153, 8)
Shape of y_train: (615, 1)
Shape of y_test: (153, 1)
In [3]:
# Standardization
import numpy

# calculate mu and sig using the training set
d = x_train.shape[1]
mu = numpy.mean(x_train, axis=0).reshape(1, d)
sig = numpy.std(x_train, axis=0).reshape(1, d)

# transform the training features
x_train = (x_train - mu) / (sig + 1E-6)

# transform the test features
x_test = (x_test - mu) / (sig + 1E-6)

print('test mean = ')
print(numpy.mean(x_test, axis=0))

print('test std = ')
print(numpy.std(x_test, axis=0))

In [5]:
class Worker:
    def __init__ (self, x, y):
        self.x = x # sbyd local feature matrix 
        self.y = y # sby1 local label matrix
        self.s = x.shape[0] # number of local samples
        self.d = x.shape[1] # number of features 
        self.w = numpy.zeros((d, 1))#dby1model parameter vector
        self.g = numpy.zeros((d, 1)) # dby1 gradient
        self.v = numpy.zeros((d, 1)) # dby1 momentum
        
    # Set the model parameters to the latest
    def set_param(self, w): 
        self.w = w

    # Compute the local loss
    def loss(self):
        yx = numpy.multiply(self.y, self.x) # sbyd matrix 
        yxw = numpy.dot(yx, self.w) # sby1 matrix
        vec1 = numpy.exp(-yxw) # sby1 matrix
        vec2 = numpy.log(1 + vec1) # sby1 matrix
        return numpy.sum(vec2) # loss function
    
    def objective(self, lam):
        n, d = self.x.shape
        yx = numpy.multiply(self.y, self.x) # n-by-d matrix
        yxw = numpy.dot(yx, self.w) # n-by-1 matrix
        vec1 = numpy.exp(-yxw) # n-by-1 matrix
        vec2 = numpy.log(1 + vec1) # n-by-1 matrix
        loss = numpy.mean(vec2) # scalar
        reg = lam / 2 * numpy.sum(self.w * self.w) # scalar
        return loss + reg

    # Compute the local gradient
#     def gradient(self):
#         yx = numpy.multiply(self.y, self.x) # sbyd matrix
#         yxw = numpy.dot(yx, self.w) # sby1 matrix
#         vec1 = numpy.exp(yxw) # sby1 matrix
#         vec2 = numpy.divide(yx, 1+vec1) # sbyd matrix
#         g =-numpy.sum(vec2, axis=0).reshape(self.d, 1) # dby1 matrix        
#         return g

    def gradient(self, lam):
        n, d = self.x.shape
        yx = numpy.multiply(self.y, self.x) # n-by-d matrix
        yxw = numpy.dot(yx, self.w) # n-by-1 matrix
        vec1 = numpy.exp(yxw) # n-by-1 matrix
        vec2 = numpy.divide(yx, 1+vec1) # n-by-d matrix
        vec3 = -numpy.mean(vec2, axis=0).reshape(d, 1) # d-by-1 matrix
        g = vec3 + lam * self.w
        return g
    
    def grad_descent(self, lam, stepsize, max_iter, w=None):
        n, d = self.x.shape
        objvals = numpy.zeros(max_iter) # store the objective values
        if self.w is None:
            self.w = numpy.zeros((d, 1)) # zero initialization

        for t in range(max_iter):
            objval = self.objective(lam)
            objvals[t] = objval
            print('Objective value at t=' + str(t) + ' is ' + str(objval))
            g = self.gradient(lam)
            self.w -= stepsize * g

        return self.w, objvals*n
    
    def stochastic_objective_gradient(self, xi, yi, lam):
        d = xi.shape[0]
        yx = yi * xi # 1-by-d matrix
        yxw = float(numpy.dot(yx, self.w)) # scalar

        # calculate objective function Q_i
        loss = numpy.log(1 + numpy.exp(-yxw)) # scalar
        reg = lam / 2 * numpy.sum(self.w * self.w) # scalar
        obj = loss + reg

        # calculate stochastic gradient
        g_loss = -yx.T / (1 + numpy.exp(yxw)) # d-by-1 matrix
        g = g_loss + lam * self.w # d-by-1 matrix

        return obj, g

    def sgd(self, lam, stepsize, max_epoch):
        n, d = self.x.shape
        objvals = numpy.zeros(max_epoch) # store the objective values
        if self.w is None:
            self.w = numpy.zeros((d, 1)) # zero initialization

        for t in range(max_epoch):
            # randomly shuffle the samples
            rand_indices = numpy.random.permutation(n)
            x_rand = self.x[rand_indices, :]
            y_rand = self.y[rand_indices, :]

            objval = 0 # accumulate the objective values
            for i in range(n):
                xi = x_rand[i, :] # 1-by-d matrix
                yi = float(y_rand[i, :]) # scalar
                obj, g = self.stochastic_objective_gradient(xi, yi, lam)
                objval += obj
                self.w -= stepsize * g

            stepsize *= 0.9 # decrease step size
            objval /= n
            objvals[t] = objval
            print('Objective value at epoch t=' + str(t) + ' is ' + str(objval))

        return self.w, objvals*n
In [6]:
class Server :

    def __init__ (self , m, n, d):
        self.m = m # number of worker nodes
        self.n = n # number of training samples
        self.d = d # number of features
        self.w = numpy.zeros((d, 1))##dby1model parameter vector 
        self.g = numpy.zeros((d, 1)) # dby1 gradient
        self.v = numpy.zeros((d, 1)) # dby1 momentum
        self.loss = 0 # loss function value
        self.obj = 0 # objective function value

    def broadcast(self): 
        return self.w
    # Sum the gradients and loss functions evaluated by the workers # Args:
    # grads: a list of dby1 vectors
    # losses : a list of scalars

    def aggregate(self, grads, losses): 
        self.g = numpy.zeros((self.d, 1)) 
        self.loss=0
        for k in range(self.m):
            self.g += grads[k]
            self.loss += losses[k]

    # Compute the gradient (from the loss and regularization )
#     def gradient (self, lam) :
#         self.g = self.g / self.n + lam * self.w
    def weight (self) :
        self.g = self.g / self.n

    # Compute the objective function (sum of loss and regularization )
#     def objective ( self , lam) :
#         reg = lam / 2 * numpy.sum(self.w * self.w) 
#         self.obj = self.loss / self.n + reg
#         return self.obj
    
    def objective (self) :
#         reg = lam / 2 * numpy.sum(self.w * self.w) 
        self.obj = self.loss / self.n
        return self.obj

# Update the model parameters using accelerated gradient descent # Args:
# alpha: learning rate (step size)
# beta : momentum parameter
#     def agd(self , alpha, beta): 
#         self.v = beta
#         self.v += self.g
#         self.w = alpha  self.v
In [7]:
import math
# Create a server and m worker nodes
def create_server_workers(m, x, y):
    n, d = x.shape
    s = math.floor(n/m) 
    server = Server(m, n, d) 
    workers = []
    for i in range(m):
        indices = list(range(i*s, (i+1)*s))
        worker = Worker(x[indices, :] , y[indices, :]) 
        workers.append( worker )
    return server, workers

In [9]:
lam = 1E-6 # regularization parameter 
alpha = 1E-1 # learning rate
beta = 0.9 # momentum parameter
max_epoch = 50 # number of epochs
local_epoch = 8 # number of epochs
obj_gd_8=[]

w_intial = server.broadcast()

for t in range(max_epoch): 
    print('round = ' + str(t))
    # step 1: broadcast
    w_global = server.broadcast()
    for i in range(m):
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        
    # step 2: workers local computations
    grads = []
    losses = []
    ws = []
    for i in range(m):
        print("worker = " + str(i))
#       g = workers[i].gradient() 
#       l = workers[i].loss()
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        w, objvals_gd = workers[i].grad_descent(lam, alpha, local_epoch)
        losses.append(objvals_gd)
        ws.append(w)
#         grads.append(g)
        
    # step 3: aggregate the workers outputs
    server.aggregate(ws, losses)
    
    # step 4: server update the model parameters
    server.weight() # compute gradient
    obj_gd_8_all = server.objective() #  compute objective function 
    obj_gd_8.append(obj_gd_8_all[-1])
    print( 'Objective_function_value = ' + str(obj_gd_8[-1]))
    print(len(obj_gd_8))

#     print( 'Objective_function_value = ' + str(obj_gd_8[-1]))
#     server.agd(alpha, beta) # updates the model parameters

50
In [10]:
lam = 1E-6 # regularization parameter 
alpha = 1E-1 # learning rate
beta = 0.9 # momentum parameter
max_epoch = 50 # number of epochs
local_epoch = 1 # number of epochs
obj_gd_1 = []

server , workers = create_server_workers(m, x_train , y_train )

for t in range(max_epoch): 
    print('round = ' + str(t))
    # step 1: broadcast
    w_global = server.broadcast()
    for i in range(m):
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        
    # step 2: workers local computations
    grads = []
    losses = []
    ws = []

    for i in range(m):
        print("worker = " + str(i))
#       g = workers[i].gradient() 
#       l = workers[i].loss()
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        w, objvals_gd = workers[i].grad_descent(lam, alpha, local_epoch)
        losses.append(objvals_gd)
        ws.append(w)
#         grads.append(g)
        
    # step 3: aggregate the workers outputs
    server.aggregate(ws, losses)
    
    # step 4: server update the model parameters
    server.weight() # compute gradient
    obj_gd_1_all = server.objective() #  compute objective function
    obj_gd_1.append(obj_gd_1_all[-1])
    print( 'Objective_function_value = ' + str(obj_gd_1[-1]))
#     server.agd(alpha, beta) # updates the model parameters

In [11]:
lam = 1E-6 # regularization parameter 
alpha = 1E-1 # learning rate
beta = 0.9 # momentum parameter
max_epoch = 50 # number of epochs
local_epoch = 8 # number of epochs
obj_sgd_8 = []


server , workers = create_server_workers(m, x_train , y_train )

for t in range(max_epoch): 
    print('round = ' + str(t))
    # step 1: broadcast
    w_global = server.broadcast()
    for i in range(m):
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        
    # step 2: workers local computations
    grads = []
    losses = []
    ws = []
    
    
    for i in range(m):
        print("worker = " + str(i))
#       g = workers[i].gradient() 
#       l = workers[i].loss()
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        w, objvals_gd = workers[i].sgd(lam, alpha, local_epoch)
        losses.append(objvals_gd)
        ws.append(w)
#         grads.append(g)
        
    # step 3: aggregate the workers outputs
    server.aggregate(ws, losses)
    
    # step 4: server update the model parameters
    server.weight() # compute gradient
    obj_sgd_8_all = server.objective() # compute compute objective function 
    obj_sgd_8.append(obj_sgd_8_all[-1])
    print( 'Objective_function_value = ' + str(obj_sgd_8[-1]))
#     server.agd(alpha, beta) # updates the model parameters

In [12]:
lam = 1E-6 # regularization parameter 
alpha = 1E-1 # learning rate
beta = 0.9 # momentum parameter
max_epoch = 50 # number of epochs
local_epoch = 8 # number of epochs
obj_sgd_1 = []

server , workers = create_server_workers(m, x_train , y_train )

for t in range(max_epoch): 
    print('round = ' + str(t))
    # step 1: broadcast
    w_global = server.broadcast()
    for i in range(m):
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        
    # step 2: workers local computations
    grads = []
    losses = []
    ws = []
    
    
    for i in range(m):
        print("worker = " + str(i))
#       g = workers[i].gradient() 
#       l = workers[i].loss()
        workers[i].set_param(w_global)
        w, objvals_gd = workers[i].sgd(lam, alpha, local_epoch)
        losses.append(objvals_gd)
        ws.append(w)
#         grads.append(g)
        
    # step 3: aggregate the workers outputs
    server.aggregate(ws, losses)
    
    # step 4: server update the model parameters
    server.weight() # compute gradient
    obj_sgd_1_all = server.objective() # compute compute objective function 
    obj_sgd_1.append(obj_sgd_1_all[-1])
    print( 'Objective_function_value = ' + str(obj_sgd_1[-1]))
#     server.agd(alpha, beta) # updates the model parameters

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
%matplotlib inline

fig = plt.figure(figsize=(6, 4))

epochs_gd_1 = range(len(obj_gd_1))
epochs_gd_8 = range(len(obj_gd_8))
epochs_sgd_1 = range(len(obj_sgd_1))
epochs_sgd_8 = range(len(obj_sgd_8))

print(epochs_gd_1)
print(epochs_gd_8)
print(epochs_sgd_1)
print(epochs_sgd_8)

line0, = plt.plot(epochs_gd_1, obj_gd_1, '--b', LineWidth=2)
line1, = plt.plot(epochs_gd_8, obj_gd_8, '-r', LineWidth=2)
line2, = plt.plot(epochs_sgd_1, obj_sgd_1, '*b', LineWidth=2)
line3, = plt.plot(epochs_sgd_8, obj_sgd_8, '*r', LineWidth=2)
plt.xlabel('Epochs', FontSize=20)
plt.ylabel('Objective Value', FontSize=20)
plt.xticks(FontSize=16)
plt.yticks(FontSize=16)
plt.legend([line0, line1, line2, line3], ['GD_1', 'GD_8','SGD_1','SGD_8'], fontsize=20)
plt.tight_layout()
plt.show()
fig.savefig('compare_gd_sgd.pdf', format='pdf', dpi=1200)
